{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"Explore new sites, relive old hikes for National Park Week","link":"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/arts-culture/explore-new-sites-relive-old-hikes-national-park-week/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>Every year, I try to visit a new National Park, or at least start planning my trip to one. That’s a little more difficult right now, but given that it’s National Park Week, I decided to try and keep with my tradition by using Google tools to satisfy my wanderlust.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <h3>Explore new places and parks</h3>\n  <p></p>\n  <p>This year, I’m heading to&nbsp;<a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/project/national-park-service?utm_source=blog.google&amp;utm_medium=post&amp;utm_campaign=national-parks\">g.co/nationalparks,</a> a Google Arts &amp; Culture project developed in collaboration with National Park Service that takes you on guided tours narrated by park rangers from the Kenai Fjords, Hawai'i Volcanoes, Carlsbad Caverns, Bryce Canyon and Dry Tortugas. I can also visit historical sites that I’ve never been to before, like <a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/exhibit/virtual-tour-of-the-eleanor-roosevelt-national-historic-site/4gLCx0_hc_fpKg\">Eleanor Roosevelt’s woodsy home</a> in Hyde Park, New York or <a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/exhibit/camping-in-nature-s-laboratory-with-thomas-edison/IAJyi-hAK4E9Lw\">Thomas Edison</a>’s camping sites (which, to me, look a little more like glamping). There are <a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/search/streetview?project=national-park-service\">more than 100 Street View historical tours</a> to choose from, and collections that let you discover Native American <a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/partner/grand-teton-national-park\">craft work or</a>&nbsp;<a href=\"https://artsandculture.google.com/partner/dinosaur-national-monument\">fossils</a> from archeological digs.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p></p>\n  <p>Afterward, I’ll take an in-depth tour of some of the <a href=\"https://earth.google.com/web/@34.7325599,-94.20828246,312.21005962a,12000000d,35y,0h,0t,0r/data=Ci0SKxIgMzVhNjc1YmQ0NjVjMTFlOTg0Yjg1NTMyNWRjMDk2MzQiB3ZveV90b2M\">National Parks of the United States</a> and wander through a few of the <a href=\"https://earth.google.com/web/@40.66685923,-97.89663015,3450a,17648333d,35y,0h,0t,0r/data=Ci4SLBIgZTRjZGJlNDAzNmViMTFlOTg5ZDAxNTBlY2RmNWE5Y2QiCG92ZXJ2aWV3\">most-loved ones</a> recommended by our community of Local Guides in two popular Google Earth Voyager stories. I plan on rounding out the week with a <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLLW-qoCMKQswJPruu9RbV4OaOMqYNLSQz\">new YouTube series</a> from the Google Earth team that travels to National Parks across the country, literally “zooming” you into places like Elephant Hill in Canyonlands National Park and Kanarraville Falls in Zion National Park. There’s even a new <a href=\"https://earth.google.com/web/@51.098014,5.727533,-15617a,26717122d,35y,0h,9t,0r/data=CisSKRIgMDhhMTY1Y2M3NWMwMTFlYWJkNDA4N2NjM2YxY2QyMTYiBXNwbC0w\">Global National Parks quiz</a> to test your geo-knowledge.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-video\">\n <div class=\"h-c-page h-c-page--mobile-full-bleed\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <div class=\"h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col-l--12 \">\n    <div class=\"article-module article-video \">\n     <figure>\n      <a class=\"h-c-video h-c-video--marquee \" data-glue-modal-disabled-on-mobile=\"true\" data-glue-modal-trigger=\"uni-modal-j_My9P_cTEs-\" href=\"https://youtube.com/watch?v=j_My9P_cTEs\"><img alt=\"Video showing a tour of Utah's National Parks.\" src=\"https://img.youtube.com/vi/j_My9P_cTEs/maxresdefault.jpg\" />\n       <svg class=\"h-c-video__play h-c-icon h-c-icon--color-white\" role=\"img\">\n        <use xlink:href=\"#mi-youtube-icon\"></use>\n       </svg></a>\n     </figure>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"h-c-modal--video uni-video-tracker\" data-analytics=\"{\n        &quot;event&quot;: &quot;page interaction&quot;,\n        &quot;category&quot;: &quot;video tracking&quot;,\n        &quot;label&quot;: &quot; - https://youtube.com/watch?v=j_My9P_cTEs&quot;\n      }\" data-glue-modal=\"uni-modal-j_My9P_cTEs-\" data-glue-modal-close-label=\"Close Dialog\">\n  <a class=\"glue-yt-video \" data-glue-yt-video-autoplay=\"true\" data-glue-yt-video-height=\"99%\" data-glue-yt-video-listeners=\"videoTrackerCtrl.listenerMap\" data-glue-yt-video-vid=\"j_My9P_cTEs\" data-glue-yt-video-width=\"100%\" href=\"https://youtube.com/watch?v=j_My9P_cTEs\" ng-cloak=\"\"></a>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>All of these things help an outdoor enthusiast who’s stuck inside (for the time being) to find unknown landscapes or get inspiration for their next trip. Perhaps for the most well-traveled out there, they’re a way to remember a favorite adventure.&nbsp;<br /><br /></p>\n  <h3>Or revisit old favorites</h3>\n  <p>Before I venture into the unknown, I decided to take a trip down memory lane (or rather, memory trail), and re-experience some of my favorite hikes in National Parks with the help of Google Street View, and anyone can join me—starting with <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@36.0646562,-112.1376312,3a,75y,14.68h,93.43t/data=!3m6!1e1!3m4!1s8A1Vq-AFa_ml0Q-jIQYxZA!2e0!7i13312!8i6656\">Bright Angel Trail</a> in the Grand Canyon. Saving the uphill journey for the second half of a hike is something my legs will never forget, but it remains one of my favorite National Parks memories. And thanks to Street View, I can recreate the journey … with fewer water breaks, probably.</p>\n  <p>I can also make my way up <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@42.9099312,-122.1328337,2a,75y,219.93h,90t/data=!3m10!1e1!3m8!1snbTmQ2lKWhXFglFbfUM7oA!2e0!6s%2F%2Fgeo3.ggpht.com%2Fcbk%3Fpanoid%3DnbTmQ2lKWhXFglFbfUM7oA%26output%3Dthumbnail%26cb_client%3Dmaps_sv.tactile.gps%26thumb%3D2%26w%3D203%26h%3D100%26yaw%3D215.23961%26pitch%3D0%26thumbfov%3D100!7i13312!8i6656!9m2!1b1!2i50\">Garfield Peak</a> in Crater Lake National Park (which I hiked during a camping trip where I first met my husband) and make as many nostalgic pit stops along the way as I want.</p>\n  <p>And last summer, my family and I all vacationed in Acadia National Park. Now that we can’t physically see one another, I’m even more grateful we went. One of my favorite memories was hiking along the park’s easternmost edge, the <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@44.3264532,-68.1775051,3a,75y,117.85h,69.84t/data=!3m6!1e1!3m4!1s8TJ_JV_AplKyrUxwTkZdWA!2e0!7i13312!8i6656\">Great Head Trail</a>, with my husband and meeting my family on <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/place/Sand+Beach/@44.329034,-68.1832339,18z/data=!3m1!4b1!4m5!3m4!1s0x4caeb94012029f19:0x412d5867d3464995!8m2!3d44.3292049!4d-68.181973\">Sand Beach</a>, a journey I’m happily retaking via Street View … and maybe on our weekly family video call, we’ll all “hike” it together.</p>\n <a href=\"https://assets.kpmg/content/dam/kpmg/it/pdf/2020/01/Global-customer-experience-excellence-2019.pdf\">loyalty to the brands</a> that make it easy to purchase products and services and connect with their customer support. Google has built digital tools to help brands do this, including the <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/see-your-messages-local-businesses-google-maps/\">ability to message</a> customers through Google Maps and Search, via Google My Business. Messaging has become such a valuable way to connect with customers that twice as many businesses are messaging via Google now, compared to last year.</p>\n  <p>Today we’re expanding <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/business-communications/business-messages\">Business Messages</a> in Maps and Search to support all kinds of businesses, and giving them the ability to integrate Business Messages directly with their customer service platforms. Business Messages provides brands a comprehensive messaging solution across Android devices, and through Maps on iOS. To improve connections with customers, we’ve recently introduced new smart replies, visual product carousels, and unique welcome messages. There’s also a smooth transition from automated replies to a customer service agent, so that it's not disruptive when the customer messages a business.</p>\n  <p>Several organizations, including Woolworths, Walmart and MyGov were among the first to try the updated Business Messages experience to make customer care more effective and efficient, particularly during COVID-19. Woolworths, Australia's largest supermarket, allows customers to search for products and see availability and aisle information at their local store, plus get details about hours and COVID-19 related updates to make shopping easier. In just a few messages, Walmart lets customers quickly find up-to-date information about store hours, pick-up and delivery options, precautions and more. And MyGov, with partner Amplify.ai, is providing help and answering live questions from Indian citizens about hours, COVID-19 helplines, and ways to volunteer and donate, for more than 11,000 food and night shelters across India. <br /></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_carousel\">\n <div class=\"h-c-page article-module\">\n  <div class=\"article-module glue-pagination h-c-carousel And through Google for Startups Accelerator for Black Founders, we’re starting our work with the first cohort of 12 startups.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <h3>Making Search and Maps more inclusive<br /></h3>\n  <p>With this attribute, our goal is to make Search and Maps more inclusive and help support Black-owned businesses when they need it most.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>“Everyone who comes into this store is welcome,” says Janet Jones, founder and co-owner of the Detroit-based Source Booksellers. “For us, being Black-owned means serving the community we’re in.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>By adding the attribute, people using Google Search and Maps can see Source Booksellers is Black-owned, and easily extend their support by purchasing one of their products, leaving a great review and sharing their Business Profile with others looking for their next book.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--medium h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--4 h-c-grid__col--offset-4 \">\n    <img alt=\"BoBA Mobile UI Pop-Up.png\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/BoBA_Mobile_UI_Pop-Up.max-2800x2800_OKaW0a.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n    <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n     <div class=\"rich-text\">\n      <p>Identity attributes are featured on merchants' Business Profiles when they opt in</p>\n     </div>\n    </figcaption>\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>To help get the word out about the new Black-owned attribute, we’ve partnered with the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://usblackchambers.org/\">U.S. Black Chambers, Inc.</a>&nbsp;(USBC). In London, where my family and I live, we’re trying to figure out what that looks like for us. We have a toddler, so our ideal day trip is somewhere she can run around and we can have a picnic—and where the public restrooms have reopened (or, failing that, a discreet wooded area…).&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>So how do I find a destination that checks all our boxes? Here’s what’s worked.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph_with_image\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid uni-paragraph-wrap\">\n   <div class=\"uni-paragraph h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--8 h-c-grid__col-m--6 h-c-grid__col-l--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-2 h-c-grid__col-m--offset-3 h-c-grid__col-l--offset-3\" data-component=\"uni-article-paragraph\">\n    <figure class=\"article-image--wrap-small \">\n     <img alt=\"Screenshot of Weald Country Park Google Maps listing\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Screenshot_20200728-145333.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n     <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n      <div class=\"rich-text\">\n       <p><br /></p>\n      </div>\n     </figcaption>\n    </figure>\n    <div class=\"rich-text\">\n     <h3>Meet at a fun halfway point</h3>\n     <p>My cousin and her family live about a two-hour drive from us, and when lockdown lifted we were more than ready to meet up. But instead of driving all the way to them—a four-hour round trip is a struggle for even the most patient of toddlers—we had the idea to meet up at a halfway point.&nbsp;</p>\n     <br />\n     <p>But how do you find that halfway point? That space between us was a no-man’s land where neither of us knew of any parks or nature reserves or anywhere that would be suitable for two energetic toddlers. So I used Google Maps to find the rough halfway point. Then I filtered by “Attractions” (you can also choose “Parks” or “Restaurants” or other categories) to see what came up. I quickly landed on <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/place/Weald+Country+Park/@51.6253265,0.2608318,15z/data=!4m5!3m4!1s0x0:0x466d8c86a72be4df!8m2!3d51.6253265!4d0.2608318\">Weald Country Park</a>, which boasts a 4.5-star rating, almost a thousand reviews and a promising description: “Fallow deer, a visitor center &amp; hiking.”</p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph_with_image\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid uni-paragraph-wrap\">\n   <div class=\"uni-paragraph h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--8 h-c-grid__col-m--6 h-c-grid__col-l--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-2 h-c-grid__col-m--offset-3 h-c-grid__col-l--offset-3\" data-component=\"uni-article-paragraph\">\n    <figure class=\"article-image--wrap-small \">\n     <img alt=\"Screenshot of reviews of Weald Country Park.png\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Screenshot_20200728-145432.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n     <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n      <div class=\"rich-text\">\n       <p><br /></p>\n      </div>\n     </figcaption>\n    </figure>\n    <div class=\"rich-text\">\n     <h3>Read the reviews</h3>\n     <p>Deer-watching had the potential to keep toddlers occupied for at least one minute. A visitor center indicated parking and bathrooms. And hiking probably meant that picnicking was easily an option. But to double-check these critical questions, I relied on the kindness of strangers who had posted recent reviews and ratings. Local Guides and other people who contribute to Google Maps are very helpful in offering information about how much they liked (or didn’t like) their trip, and many of them have the same topics on their mind that I do. Since you can sort reviews by date, it was easy to see the most relevant ones—i.e., those that have been filed since lockdown lifted—for current info on toilets (yes), parking (yes, but it’s expensive), and whether the playgrounds have reopened (yes, very recently).&nbsp;</p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph_with_image\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid uni-paragraph-wrap\">\n   <div class=\"uni-paragraph h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--8 h-c-grid__col-m--6 h-c-grid__col-l--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-2 h-c-grid__col-m--offset-3 h-c-grid__col-l--offset-3\" data-component=\"uni-article-paragraph\">\n    <figure class=\"article-image--wrap-small \">\n     <img alt=\"screenshot of photos from Weald Country Park.png\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Screenshot_20200728-145528.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n     <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n      <div class=\"rich-text\">\n       <p><br /></p>\n      </div>\n     </figcaption>\n    </figure>\n    <div class=\"rich-text\">\n     <h3>Browse the photos and Street View</h3>\n     <p>To really get a feel for a place, sometimes there’s no replacement for a photo. Happily, many Google Maps contributors feel the same way, so it’s often very easy to find recent photos of the places you’re thinking of visiting. And for a 360-degree panorama, I can drop the pin and check out the scene on Street View. Maps","link":"https://blog.google/products/maps/better-local-recommendations-google-maps/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>More than a billion people turn to Google Maps to navigate and explore the world and their communities. And thanks to the hundreds of millions people who contribute information to Google Maps each year—like the best takeaway dish to order at a local restaurant or a photo of a nearby park’s new open hours—people can get local recommendations and up-to-date information about where to go and what to do. We’re now making it easier to uncover community-powered updates and recommendations in Google Maps.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Last year we <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/discover-new-places-with-help-from-local-guides/\">announced</a> a Google Maps pilot feature that allowed people to follow select <a href=\"https://maps.google.com/localguides/\">Local Guides</a>, the everyday people who are passionate about sharing their experiences on Google Maps. It was exciting to see many of the Local Guides we invited in our initial pilot opt in and participate. Equally exciting was the interest we saw from many Google Maps users who began following top Local Guides to receive helpful recommendations about the places around them.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Today we’re expanding this feature and beginning to roll it out globally. If a Google Maps user has shared photos, reviews or lists publicly, you can now follow them and get their recommendations, advice and updates delivered to your Updates tab in Google Maps. So the next time you find someone sharing helpful photos of takeout menus, handy lists of your city's most spacious parks or inspiring photos of local shops and services, you can keep up-to-date on all of their recommendations.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--medium h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--4 h-c-grid__col--offset-4 \">\n    <img alt=\"Google Maps public profile\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Google_Maps_public_profile_UI.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n    <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n     <div class=\"rich-text\">\n      <p>Topic filters add color and flavor to your Google Maps profile</p>\n     </div>\n    </figcaption>\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>There will also be new topic filters on Google Maps profiles, so you can see the topics and places people share about the most, like pizza, brunch, camping and parks. Whether they’re a coffee enthusiast documenting every last latte, or a hometown expert reviewing all things Perth or Phoenix, you can follow other Google Maps users with public profiles to get helpful recommendations about the places around you.</p>\n  <br />\n  <h3>Control your Google Maps experience and profile</h3>\n  <p>People want to be in control of their digital footprint. That’s why we’ve built in settings so you can easily manage and personalize your Google Maps profile. As always, everyone has the option to show (or not show) their reviews, photos and posts on their public Maps profile. To become followable in Google Maps, an eligible user can go to their profile and follow a simple process. And users who are followable on Google Maps can make their profile restricted. With a restricted profile, you approve new followers before they can see contributions on your profile.&nbsp;</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Want to share your personality on your Google Maps profile? Create a short tagline that sparks a sense of adventure. Or simply drop in a pasta emoji if there are no words to describe how much you love Italian food.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_carousel\">\n <div class=\"h-c-page article-module\">\n With a simple drag-and-drop interface you can add placemarks, draw lines and shapes, and embed text, photos and videos. You can share your map via public URL, embed it on websites or publish your map for others to see.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Over the past four months, we’ve seen a surge in the number of people creating and viewing My Maps. From December 2019 to April 2020, we saw nearly a billion more My Maps creations, edits and views compared to the same time period last year, growing from 2 billion to nearly 3 billion. With My Maps, communities have been sharing helpful, local information in rapidly changing situations—from COVID-19 testing sites and food banks to where first responders can access <a href=\"https://dfs.wyo.gov/services/family-services/child-care/essential-personnel-childcare/\">childcare facilities</a>.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <h3>Maps can help us and our communities stay safe</h3>\n  <p>A map can be helpful in ways that a simple list of text is not: it helps us instantly see information in the context of where we are, with the locations of the resources we might need.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <figure class=\"article-image--full article-module \">\n  <img alt=\"My Maps animation\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/MM_Animation.gif\" />\n </figure>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>With My Maps, anyone can be a cartographer. People can import their own data into a custom map, similar to how the San Francisco Department of Homelessness &amp; Supportive Housing mapped downtown <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/d/u/0/viewer?ll=37.77251031480697%2C-122.42804134159735&amp;z=14&amp;mid=1jCE9lI8Iv12tO-wWrF6RIQPWKXGBK0_z\">hand-washing and hygiene stations</a> to support hand hygiene and reduce the spread of COVID-19. With a spreadsheet or <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/kml\">KML</a> you can have your own custom map in no time.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Some maps take a bit more than hand-drawn points and polygons. For that, My Maps creators can import their own mapping data and mash it up with other sources.&nbsp;</p>\n  <br />For example, the online newspaper Briarcliff Daily Voice created a My Map showing the \n  <a href=\"https://dailyvoice.com/new-york/briarcliff/news/covid-19-daily-voices-interactive-map-of-nyc-metro-area-cases/785327/\">spread of coronavirus cases</a> in the New York City metropolitan area, using data from three state healthcare agencies and the city’s health department. Pennsylvania.gov has leveraged My Maps to inform Pennsylvanians about coronavirus \n  <a href=\"https://www.pa.gov/guides/responding-to-covid-19/#CasesinPennsylvania\">cases by county</a>. And The Chicago Sun-Times has a map showing \n  <a href=\"https://chicago.suntimes.com/coronavirus/2020/3/24/21191831/map-heres-where-to-get-tested-coronavirus-chicago-illinois-covid-19\">where to get tested</a> for coronavirus in the Chicago area.\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <figure class=\"article-image--full article-module \">\n  <img alt=\"Food bank\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Food_bank.max-1000x1000.jpg\" />\n </figure>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <h3>Anyone can be a force for good with simple, easy-to-use maps</h3>\n  <p>In the past few months, we've seen how powerful this small set of relatively simple features can be. People are using My Maps to to be forces for good and coordinate relief efforts.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Map by map, people are connecting each other to resources for caring for ourselves and others, while staying healthy and informed. We’re seeing everyone from members of Congress to local nonprofits use Google My Maps to visualize information like <a href=\"https://meals4kids.org/school-closure-meal-information\">school lunch pick-up spots</a>&nbsp;to the spread of the virus in our communities.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>Here are 10 helpful My Maps we’ve seen developed by communities around the world:</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"Street View is helping this tour guide stay in business","link":"https://blog.google/products/maps/street-view-helping-tour-guide-stay-business/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>On March 24, government restrictions due to COVID-19 went into effect across the United Kingdom. With nonessential businesses forced to close, public gatherings banned, and most people required to stay at home, these regulations instantly transformed daily life. They also presented a serious threat to Katie Wignall’s business: Katie makes her living as a tour guide, showing curious visitors the highlights of London.</p>\n  <p>But instead of trying to simply wait out the crisis, Katie looked to technology for a solution to creatively keep her business going. We chatted with her to find out how she’s successfully managed to take her walking tours virtual.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph_with_image\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid uni-paragraph-wrap\">\n   <div class=\"uni-paragraph h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--8 h-c-grid__col-m--6 h-c-grid__col-l--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-2 h-c-grid__col-m--offset-3 h-c-grid__col-l--offset-3\" data-component=\"uni-article-paragraph\">\n    <figure class=\"article-image--wrap-small \">\n     <img alt=\"Beaver statues on London's Oxford Street\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Beavers_on_Oxford_Street.max-1000x1000.jpg\" />\n     <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n      <div class=\"rich-text\">\n       <p>One of the beaver statues on Oxford Street</p>\n      </div>\n     </figcaption>\n    </figure>\n    <div class=\"rich-text\">\n     <p><b>Describe your business, <a href=\"https://lookup.london/\">Look Up London</a>.</b></p>\n     <p>I provide walking tours all over London for public and private groups. I’m a <a href=\"https://www.itg.org.uk/about/how-to-become-a-tourist-guide/\">Blue Badge Tourist Guide</a>, which is the top accreditation for tourist guides in the UK. We do two years of training, pass 11 exams, and we’re the only guides that can take you inside the Tower of London and Westminster Abbey.</p>\n     <p>Look Up London started originally as a <a href=\"https://lookup.london/blog/\">blog</a> and <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/look_uplondon/\">social media channels</a>, where I shared quirkier bits of London history. The name is all about spotting the little details in the architecture around you, to tell the story of why something looks the way it does. For example, on Oxford Street, which is famous for its shopping, there's a building decorated with sculptures of beavers. They're a clue to the fact it used to be a hat factory—slightly gruesome, but a detail that is so often missed by passersby!</p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>How has your business been impacted by COVID-19 and the government restrictions?</b></p>\n  <p>I’ve had to shut down, basically. I can’t go out; we’re not able to meet up in groups to deliver the normal tours. All of the work I had booked going into the summer—the busiest time—has just been cancelled or postponed. Literally overnight there was no work at all.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph_with_image\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid uni-paragraph-wrap\">\n   <div class=\"uni-paragraph h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--8 h-c-grid__col-m--6 h-c-grid__col-l--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-2 h-c-grid__col-m--offset-3 h-c-grid__col-l--offset-3\" data-component=\"uni-article-paragraph\">\n    <figure class=\"article-image--wrap-small \">\n     <img alt=\"Katie Wignall giving a tour of London's Guildhall\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Photo_27-03-2020_17_47_30.max-1000x1000.jpg\" />\n     <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n      <div class=\"rich-text\">\n       <p>Katie giving a tour of the Guildhall</p>\n      </div>\n     </figcaption>\n    </figure>\n    <div class=\"rich-text\">\n     <p><b>What gave you the idea for virtual tours?</b></p>\n     <p>It was actually a suggestion from a follower on Instagram who asked, “Is there a way you could do virtual tours?” I started out by going out myself and having my husband film me on London streets, but then as the situation escalated, we weren’t allowed outside.</p>\n     <p>So then I thought I’d experiment with <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@51.5019149,-0.1414768,3a,75y,200.13h,91.71t/data=!3m6!1e1!3m4!1s1wKqv1jXMpgdSjUlQajfyA!2e0!7i13312!8i6656\">Google Street View</a>. If I couldn’t go outside, I could offer people the next best thing, through a screen. I was already using Street View a lot for my work—it’s really good for my research. I love the feature where you can go back in time. It’s not possible for every location, but for a lot of central London, you can select a place in Google Maps for desktop, drag the Street View pegman into the picture and click on the clock in the top left corner to <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lvH3rtFMa9o\">explore imagery from the past</a>. You can see where buildings have been demolished and what used to be standing where.</p>So now, every Monday, Wednesday and Friday at 2 PM London time, I use Street View to give a virtual tour on Instagram Live. And for anyone who can’t make that time, I post the recordings \n     <a href=\"https://lookup.london/live/\">on my website</a>. They’re all free, and if people enjoy them, they can make a donation.\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>What’s been the response?</b></p>\n  <p>People have been so lovely. From the comments, I think it’s been very helpful for people in lockdown, who maybe are older and can’t get out of the house as often, or people who’ve had to leave London and are feeling homesick. Lots have messaged me to say it’s made them feel like they’ve been outside. They’ve really learned something new and taken their minds off the situation for twenty minutes or so.</p>\n  <p><b>Any advantages to using Street View compared to being there in person?</b></p>\n  <p>The great thing about Street View is that you can hop about—you can jump a mile down the road and people don’t have to get on a bus or actually walk, so you can cover a lot of ground.</p>\n  <p>And then there’s that feature to go back in time and see things how they appeared years ago, back to 2008. On a normal tour, you can show pictures and give people an idea, but if people are on Street View and feel like they’re standing in a space and seeing the changes right there, it’s a different experience.</p>\n  <p>One example, on <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=252299472479782\">my Aldgate tour</a>, is a garden space that has been relandscaped. The garden looks beautiful now, but three years ago you could see the cobbles of Victorian London. And those cobbles happen to have been the site of the murder of Catherine Eddowes, who was a victim of Jack the Ripper. That was an evocative thing to be able to show.</p>\n  <p><b>Any advice for other small business owners who are trying to figure out how to adapt right now?</b></p>\n  <p>I think you have to do the thing that you enjoy doing. I don’t think I’d be able to do these three times a week if I didn’t enjoy them. If you have something that you want to share, there’s no reason you shouldn’t do that. Technology has made everything so accessible, and if you care about something, chances are others care about that as well.</p>\n </div>\n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Fri, 24 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"Porsche Taylor puts women in the driver's seat","link":"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/diversity/porsche-taylor-women-riders-world-relay/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>Porsche Taylor’s first time riding a motorcycle alone could have gone better. “That first ride, I had absolutely nothing on right: My helmet was too big, I didn’t own a jacket. I might have had on some baseball gloves; everything was just totally upside-down wrong,” she says. “But I wasn’t afraid, it was exhilarating. It was trying something new, being in control. It was that initial feeling of the freedom of the wind.”</p>\n  <p>Porsche was one of the participants in the <a href=\"https://womenridersworldrelay.com/\">Women Riders World Relay</a>, a relay ride that spanned the globe, beginning in February 2019 in Scotland and ending February 2020 in London. <a href=\"http://goo.gle/womenriders\">WRWR organizers used Google products</a> like Maps, Sheets and Translate to make sure riders not only had constant, up-to-date access to their routes, but also were able to explore and connect with one another along the way.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-video\">\n <div class=\"h-c-page h-c-page--mobile-full-bleed\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <div class=\"h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col-l--12 \">\n    <div class=\"article-module article-video \">\n     <figure>\n      <a class=\"h-c-video h-c-video--marquee \" data-glue-modal-disabled-on-mobile=\"true\" data-glue-modal-trigger=\"uni-modal-FldLWuBibuw-\" href=\"https://youtube.com/watch?v=FldLWuBibuw\"><img alt=\"Video showing women riding motorcycles across the world.\" src=\"https://img.youtube.com/vi/FldLWuBibuw/maxresdefault.jpg\" />\n       <svg class=\"h-c-video__play h-c-icon h-c-icon--color-white\" role=\"img\">\n        <use xlink:href=\"#mi-youtube-icon\"></use>\n       </svg></a>\n     </figure>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"h-c-modal--video uni-video-tracker\" data-analytics=\"{\n        &quot;event&quot;: &quot;page interaction&quot;,\n        &quot;category&quot;: &quot;video tracking&quot;,\n        &quot;label&quot;: &quot; - https://youtube.com/watch?v=FldLWuBibuw&quot;\n      }\" data-glue-modal=\"uni-modal-FldLWuBibuw-\" data-glue-modal-close-label=\"Close Dialog\">\n  <a class=\"glue-yt-video \" data-glue-yt-video-autoplay=\"true\" data-glue-yt-video-height=\"99%\" data-glue-yt-video-listeners=\"videoTrackerCtrl.listenerMap\" data-glue-yt-video-vid=\"FldLWuBibuw\" data-glue-yt-video-width=\"100%\" href=\"https://youtube.com/watch?v=FldLWuBibuw\" ng-cloak=\"\"></a>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>“The whole team did phenomenally with the amount of time they had to put together the route and figure out the baton passes,” says Porsche. Google Maps was particularly useful for creating Porsche’s route. She and her fellow riders rode from Sept. 25 to Oct. 14, starting in Maine and heading west across the Canadian border, then down through the Southwest to the Mexican border in Texas. They crossed the country, occasionally riding through snowstorms and dropping temperatures. “When you consider the seasons we were riding through, it was a definite challenge for organizers to find routes that weren’t closed down.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>While Google Maps could help the riders along their journey, it couldn’t do anything about inclement weather. “I quit about four times,” laughs Porsche. “Riding in the cold is not my favorite thing to do. But it was a positive experience all the way around; I don’t know that I would ride in the freezing cold again, but I would do a ride with those women again for sure. I always say the bonds are built on the ground: You’re going to love the folks you ride with to death or you won’t be so cool, and I’m happy to say I love those ladies to death.”</p>\n  <p>Porsche is vocal about the need for more representation for women in the motor sports community, and she says that things like social media visibility and technical tools like Google Hangouts have helped women who may have felt alone in their shared passion find each other. This idea is in part what inspired her to found <a href=\"http://blackgirlsride.com/\">Black Girls Ride</a>, a magazine and community originally launched as a place for women of color who ride, which has since grown to include all women. What inspired her to launch Black Girls Ride was the lack of representation she saw when she first started riding—especially in long-distance riding. Traditionally, women filled support roles during these cross-country expeditions, taking a literal backseat to men. In fact, Porsche’s first experience on a bike was sitting behind a man, on the back of her cousin’s bike. “I didn’t so much like the feeling of being a passenger...but I loved the feeling of riding.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Thanks to women like Porsche and the WRWR riders, the world of motor sports is changing. “Women have become fearless and bold enough to take long distance biking trips on their own. We’re witnessing the explosion of the all-female long distance ride, where women take it upon themselves to create rides that cater to them instead of being a subset of an all-male ride. It’s where we get to take our power back.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Talking about these rides and seeing women taking them via social media and internet communities are crucial, says Porsche, who also mentions using Google Hangouts to connect with riders across the country. “You’re able to see the growth of female riders; women taking these long distance trips and riding solo have always been there—there are women riding today who have been doing this since the 60s—but social media is now shining a light on them.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>That increased visibility is part of Porsche's work with Black Girls Ride. “I knew from riding in LA that there were more of us than the community would admit to. There was no representation in mainstream media, even for women who were riding professionally, there was very little to nothing,” Porsche says. Now \"women all over the world are connecting to the Black Girls Ride brand. We have readers in London, Nigeria, France, just about every country you can name. I’m motivated by these women.” Black Girls Ride has become more than a publication, hosting trainings, workshops and events. And while both men and women are included, it’s Porsche’s focus to make sure women riders are invited to the table and that they are given the same representation, advertising and sponsorship opportunities.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Most of all, she just wants women to feel welcome in this world. “It’s always been my goal to create safe spaces for women to ask questions and get the help they need without fear of ridicule,” she says. “And I’m glad I can be a part of creating that.”&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Learn more about the women behind WRWR and how they planned their relay at <a businesses are crucial to our communities. As we head into&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.un.org/en/observances/small-business-day\">International Small Business Day</a>&nbsp;on June 27, we’ve compiled six Google Maps tips anyone can use to help small businesses during the pandemic.&nbsp;</i></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>As cities and economies start to reopen, people are looking for ways to support their favorite small businesses. We recently <a href=\"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/small-business/new-tools-help-businesses-during-covid-19/\">announced</a> new features to help business owners get support, adjust operations and reach customers in new ways, and have heard from people around the world that they want to support their favorite small businesses.&nbsp;<br /></p>\n  <p>Here are six easy ways you can show support for small businesses in your community right now:<br /></p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>1. Report a place as re-opened and edit other helpful information&nbsp;</b></p>\n  <p>Business owners may not have the time or resources to keep the information on their online listing updated. If you know a business has reopened to the public, but it’s still marked as closed on Google Search or Maps, you can report it as re-opened. Click on the “Temporarily Closed” banner on the business and select “Suggest an edit” to let us know that the business has reopened. And for businesses that have reopened with different hours, you can also submit updated open hours information.<br /></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Update the Temporarily Closed label on Google Maps\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Update_Temp_Closed_label.max-1000x1000.jpg\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>2. Spread the word with reviews, ratings and photos</b></p>\n  <p>Share your experience. Writing about a restaurant’s well-executed takeout window or adding photos of the menu or dish you ordered in your Maps review can help businesses you love attract more customers.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <p></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Leave a review on Google Maps\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Leave_a_review.max-1000x1000.jpg\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>3.&nbsp;Try an online class</b></p>Missing your go-to yoga studio or in desperate need of a consultation with your hair stylist? Many businesses are pivoting to online services due to COVID-19 restrictions, and you can now see local businesses offering online classes, appointments and estimates, right on Google Search and Maps. Search using terms like “yoga classes near me,” “hair salons” or “piano lessons” to see some of the businesses near you offering these services—and even book directly on Google Search or Maps via a number of our Reserve with Google \n  <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/reserve/partners\">partners</a>.\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Book an online class with Google Maps\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Online_Class_Booking_2_1_RhqFITx.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>4.&nbsp;Buy a gift card or leave a donation</b></p>\n  <p>If you have the means, purchase a gift card or make a donation to help businesses in your community. Doing so gives business owners the funds to support employees, while reassuring them that they’ll have your business in the future.&nbsp;If you’re in the U.S., the U.K. or Canada, you can simply type \"support local businesses\" or a similar term in Google Search to see a list of businesses in your area that are accepting donations or offering gift cards. And for a limited time, you can also click the banner in your Google Maps app on your phone to find businesses near you that are looking for support.&nbsp;Businesses in more than 25 countries can now set up gift card or donation campaigns through <a href=\"https://support.google.com/business/answer/9872059\">Google My Business</a>.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Buy a Gift Card or Donate to a local business\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Buy_a_Gift_Card_or_Donate.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>5. Make a reservation for a future appointment</b></p>\n  <p>Missed reservations and skipped services are understandable these days, but they can be stressful to local business owners and employees. Consider rescheduling services and appointments for a future date so you can assure local merchants that they still have your business. Plenty of salons and other businesses take appointments and reservations directly from Search or Maps.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <p></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Book a later appointment\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Book_a_later_appointment.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>6. Order delivery or takeout</b></p>\n  <p>Many restaurants and bars that are closed for dine-in service have pivoted to takeout and delivery. If you’re not in the mood to cook, treat yourself while supporting one of your local restaurants. Use Google Maps to find restaurants around you that are offering takeout, curbside pickup, delivery, or no-contact delivery.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <p></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div COVID-19","link":"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/small-business/new-tools-help-businesses-during-covid-19/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>Running a business requires a whole lot of ingenuity and perseverance. It’s those same qualities that are helping local businesses adapt, and even thrive, in today’s new normal. To adjust, business owners are increasingly turning to digital tools. According to a <a href=\"http://digitallyempowered.connectedcouncil.org\">newly released report</a> by the Connected Commerce Council, nearly one in three small business owners said that without digital tools they would have had to close all or parts of their business.</p>\n  <p>We’ve rolled out new features to help businesses get the support they need, adapt their operations, and quickly update customers about their latest changes.</p>\n  <p><b>Let people know how they can help&nbsp;</b></p>\n  <p>We’ve seen firsthand in Google Search and Maps the impact that COVID-19 has had on small businesses and how they connect with their customers. People across the world are looking for ways to continue supporting corner bookstores, local watering holes, beloved dance studios and other businesses that give their neighborhoods character—even if it’s from a distance.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>To help local businesses share how their communities can support them during COVID-19, we recently began allowing merchants in six countries <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/outreach-initiatives/small-business/support-links-business-profile-google/\">to add support links</a> for donations and gift cards to their Business Profiles on Google. Starting today, we’re rolling support links out to merchants in an additional 18 countries such as Italy, Spain and Japan. We’ve partnered with PayPal and GoFundMe for donations. For gift cards, merchants can link directly to the relevant page on their website or to their gift card offerings with one of our eligible partners, which includes Square, Toast, Clover and Vagaro.</p>\n  <p>People around the world are looking to help—with global search interest in \"how to help small businesses\" reaching an all-time high in March 2020, increasing more than 700 percent since February. To help connect them with nearby businesses in need, we’ve made it possible for people to look up their favorite local businesses by name to see if they’ve added donation or gift card links to their Business Profile. And in the coming weeks, people will also be able to use Search and Maps to find all of the nearby businesses that are asking for support.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Support Links Search\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Support_Links_Search.gif\" />\n    <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n     <div class=\"rich-text\">\n      <p>People can now look up their favorite local businesses to see if they have donation or gift card links on their Business Profile</p>\n     </div>\n    </figcaption>\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>Transition to online services with ease&nbsp;</b></p>\n  <p>Merchants who normally provided in-person services are now pivoting to connect with their customers virtually—from yoga studios offering online classes to salons hosting virtual hair styling classes. We’re making it easier for customers to discover online classes and book virtual appointments with these new features:</p>\n  <ul>\n   <li><p><b>Get discovered:</b>Merchants who are verified on Google My Business will soon be able to add attributes like “online classes,” “online appointments,” or “online estimates” to their Business Profiles to let people know how they’re operating. Today merchants can add one of these attributes using Google My Business, and in the coming weeks it’ll be visible on merchants’ Business Profiles in Search and Maps.&nbsp;</p></li>\n  </ul>\n  <ul>\n   <li><p><b>Online service bookings directly on Google:</b>We’re expanding Reserve with Google to help merchants offer easy appointment bookings for online services so customers can quickly find available times, book a slot, and add it to their Google Calendar—all directly from a merchant’s Business Profile. Millions of people have already booked in-person appointments with salons, restaurants and other businesses thanks to integrations from over 100 Reserve with Google&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/reserve/partners\">partners</a>. We’re now expanding this to include bookings for online services, starting with partners like Booksy, Regis, WellnessLiving, and Zooty. Merchants working with one of these partners can offer online bookings directly on Google and share details with customers about how to pay and join the meeting using their preferred video platform.</p></li>\n  </ul>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--medium h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--4 h-c-grid__col--offset-4 \">\n    <img alt=\"Online Class Booking\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Online_Class_Booking_2.max-1000x1000.png\" />\n    <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n     <div class=\"rich-text\">\n      <p>&nbsp;Merchants can offer easy appointment bookings for online services.&nbsp;</p>\n     </div>\n    </figcaption>\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><b>Keep everyone in the know with the latest business information</b></p>\n  <p>Sometimes it’s not as simple as “open” and “closed.” Since the beginning of the pandemic, we’ve added new tools to help merchants keep customers informed about how and when they’re operating.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Across all business verticals, we launched the ability to mark their business as temporarily closed, as well as reopen when they’re ready to open their doors. We also added secondary hours and COVID-19 posts so merchants can communicate important information about their operations directly in Google Search and Maps. Since March, we’ve seen more than 1 million businesses share COVID-19 posts, with millions of clicks to merchants’ websites every week as consumers look for more information.</p>\n  <p>With many people unable to enjoy meals inside their favorite restaurants, demand for food delivery and takeout has skyrocketed. In response, we’ve added more third-party ordering providers, so people everywhere can order delivery and takeout from an additional 25,000 restaurants directly on Google. To give merchants even more control, we’ll soon be making it easier for food merchants to indicate their preferred online ordering partners on their Business Profiles.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Today people are deciding where to grab food not only based on the menu, but also on how easy it is to pick up safely. We added attributes like “curbside pickup,” “no contact delivery,” and “dine-in” so that restaurants could easily share these important details on their Business Profiles in Search and Maps. Since March, more than 3 million restaurants have added or edited their dining attributes. Some restaurateurs are even ditching dining areas for good. To support all types of food merchants, virtual kitchens can now verify their businesses on Google My Business.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>We know that every day during this pandemic can be drastically different—and for small business owners, there can be a lot of uncertainty. While we can’t control what each day looks like, our goal is to continue helping businesses communicate the latest with consumers across the world.&nbsp;<br /></p>\n 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"Ride easy with new biking features in Google Maps","link":"https://blog.google/products/maps/ride-easy-new-biking-features-google-maps/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>People across the world are opting to hop on their bikes—especially with summer arriving in many parts of the world and more people looking for safer ways to get around. Since February, requests for cycling directions in Google Maps have jumped by 69 percent—hitting an all-time high last month. Whether people are hitting the road to get their heart pumping or commute safely during COVID-19, we’re making it easier for cyclists everywhere to get on their own bike or a shared one.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>&nbsp;Ten years ago, we <a href=\"https://googleblog.blogspot.com/2010/03/biking-directions-added-to-google-maps.html\">introduced</a> biking directions in Google Maps. Now it’s available in nearly 30 countries around the world and millions of people use it every day. As biking habits change, especially as things evolve with COVID-19, we’re constantly updating this information to help you uncover the most reliable bike route.</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <h3>Raise the (handle)bar on biking routes&nbsp;&nbsp;</h3>\n  <p>To give you the most up-to-date bike route, we use a combination of machine learning, complex algorithms and our understanding of real-world conditions based on imagery and data from government authorities and community contributions. We also consider various forms of bike lanes and nearby streets that might be less friendly for your two wheels (like tunnels, stairs and poor surface conditions) so you can have the best and smoothest biking route. You can also see how flat or steep your route will be, so you’ll know if you’re in for an easy breezy ride or one that will really get the heart pumping.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>However, the best route can always change and we are hard at work to reflect new information. For instance, due to COVID-19, many cities are adding and widening bike lanes to encourage cycling and accommodate more riders. We’re already working to integrate hundreds of thousands of new bike lanes in the coming months. Local government agencies can provide this data through our <a href=\"https://support.google.com/mapcontentpartners/answer/9359574?hl=en\">Geo Data Upload tool</a> to have their latest bike lane information reflected in Google Maps.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p><br /></p>\n  <h3>Gear up for new docked bikeshare directions in 10 cities</h3>\n  <p>As more people choose to cycle, they’re buying new bikes, fixing up old ones and turning to bike sharing options. In fact, worldwide search interest for “bike repair near me” hit an all-time high this month—more than double what it was last year.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>For riders opting to use bike sharing, we’re rolling out more detailed information. Over the last several years, we’ve <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/travel-last-mile-google-maps-and-lime/\">launched</a> a dockless bike and scooter integration with Lime in more than 100 cities and <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/real-time-bikeshare-information-google-map/\">introduced</a> real-time docked bikeshare information to help travellers in select cities locate bike sharing stations and real-time availability. With bikeshare providers seeing sharp increases in usage during COVID-19, it’s even more important to quickly and easily check how many bikes are available at the station you’re headed toward and if there are docks available to drop off your bike near your destination.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>Starting today, when you look up biking directions, you’ll see end-to-end directions that include docked bikeshare information. Steps will include detailed walking directions to bikeshare stations near your starting point along with live bike availability, turn-by-turn cycling directions to the bikeshare station closest to your destination with live dock availability, and, finally, walking directions from there to your final destination. And, for some cities, Maps will show you links to open the relevant bikeshare app to book and unlock the bike.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"docked-bike-full.gif\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/docked-bike-full.gif\" />\n    <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption \">\n     <div class=\"rich-text\">\n      <p>New docked bikeshare directions coming to 10 cities.</p>\n     </div>\n    </figcaption>\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>Rolling out over the coming weeks, you’ll find docked bikeshare directions in these 10 cities, thanks to our partnership with <a href=\"https://www.itoworld.com/\">Ito World</a>and bikeshare partners around the world. We’re actively working with additional partners to bring this functionality to more cities in the coming months.&nbsp;</p>\n  <ul>\n   <li>Chicago, U.S. (Divvy/Lyft)</li>\n   <li>New York City, U.S. (Citi Bike/Lyft)</li>\n   <li>San Francisco Bay Area, U.S. (Bay Wheels/Lyft)</li>\n   <li>Washington, DC, U.S. (Capital Bikeshare/Lyft)</li>\n   <li>London, England (Santander Cycles/TfL)</li>\n   <li>Mexico City, Mexico (Ecobici)</li>\n   <li>Montreal, Canada (BIXI/Lyft)</li>\n   <li>Rio De Janeiro, Brazil (Bike Itaú)</li>\n   <li>São Paulo, Brazil (Bike Itaú)</li>\n   <li>Taipei and New Taipei City, Taiwan (YouBike)</li>\n  </ul>\n  <p>As with any mode of transportation right now, cleanliness and safety are top of mind. All of our bikeshare partners have taken steps to increase their cleaning protocols during COVID-19. Please check with your local partner to learn about their latest safety measures. And as always, we encourage you to follow local health and safety guidelines—no matter how you’re getting around.&nbsp;</p>\n </div>\n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Mon, 20 Jul 2020 15:00:00 +0000","feedId":591,"bgimg":"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/docked-bike-full.gif","linkMd5":"80b2af85ec5d5b308115af77c5e20f62","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/docked-bike-full.gif":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/SbSV?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn10@2020_2/2020/08/16/12-12-00-698_4bbeb52263385580.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/SbSV?i=xnUQVeWKunM:pOUYqlTNV40:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn18@2020_3/2020/08/16/12-12-00-912_8a6dca0864dcf618.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/blogspot/SbSV/~4/xnUQVeWKunM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn97@2020_2/2020/08/16/12-11-59-457_42f5e72b524143c8.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"Find wheelchair accessible places with Google Maps","link":"https://blog.google/products/maps/wheelchair-accessible-places-google-maps/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p><i>Editor’s note: Today is Global Accessibility Awareness Day, and we’ll be sharing <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/outreach-initiatives/education/global-accessibility-awareness-day-2020\">resources and tools for education</a>, as well as accessibility features and updates for <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android/accessibility-updates-help-tech-work-everyone\">Android</a> and Google Maps.&nbsp;</i></p>\n  <p>Imagine making plans to go somewhere new, taking the journey to get there and arriving— only to be stuck outside, prevented from sitting with family or being unable to access the restroom. It’s a deeply frustrating experience I’ve had many times since <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/outreach-initiatives/accessibility/wheelchair-users-google-maps/\">becoming a wheelchair user</a> in 2009. And it’s an experience all too familiar to the <a href=\"https://www.wheelchairfoundation.org/fth/analysis-of-wheelchair-need/\">130 million wheelchair users</a> worldwide and the more than <a href=\"https://www.census.gov/newsroom/releases/archives/miscellaneous/cb12-134.html\">30 million Americans</a> who have difficulty using stairs.</p>\n  <p>So imagine instead being able to “know before you go” whether a destination is wheelchair accessible, just as effortlessly as looking up the address. In recognition of <a href=\"https://globalaccessibilityawarenessday.org/\">Global Accessibility Awareness Day</a>, we’re announcing a new Google Maps feature that does just that.</p>\n  <p>People can now turn on an “Accessible Places” feature to have wheelchair accessibility information more prominently displayed in Google Maps. When Accessible Places is switched on, a wheelchair icon will indicate an accessible entrance and you’ll be able to see if a place has accessible seating, restrooms or parking. If it’s confirmed that a place does not have an accessible entrance, we’ll show that information on Maps as well.</p>\n  <p></p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-video\">\n <div class=\"h-c-page h-c-page--mobile-full-bleed\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <div class=\"h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col-l--12 \">\n    <div class=\"article-module article-video \">\n     <figure>\n      <a class=\"h-c-video h-c-video--marquee \" data-glue-modal-disabled-on-mobile=\"true\" data-glue-modal-trigger=\"uni-modal--oWsAMwJ-ks-\" href=\"https://youtube.com/watch?v=-oWsAMwJ-ks\">\n       <div class=\"article-video__aspect-image\" style=\"background-image: url(https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/images/Screen_Shot_2020-05-20_at_7.49.47_PM.max-1000x1000.png);\">\n        <span class=\"h-u-visually-hidden\">Video explaining how Accessible Places benefits everyone who uses wheels.</span>\n       </div>\n       <svg class=\"h-c-video__play h-c-icon h-c-icon--color-white\" role=\"img\">\n        <use xlink:href=\"#mi-youtube-icon\"></use>\n       </svg></a>\n     </figure>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n  </div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"h-c-modal--video uni-video-tracker\" data-analytics=\"{\n        &quot;event&quot;: &quot;page interaction&quot;,\n        &quot;category&quot;: &quot;video tracking&quot;,\n        &quot;label&quot;: &quot; That number has more than doubled since <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/building-map-everyone/\">2017</a> thanks to the dedication of more than 120 million <a href=\"https://maps.google.com/localguides/howto\">Local Guides</a>and others who’ve responded to <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/better-world-wheels-google-maps/\">our call to share accessibility information</a>. In total, this community has contributed more than 500 million wheelchair accessibility updates to Google Maps. Store owners have also helped, using Google My Business to <a href=\"https://support.google.com/business/answer/7298639?hl=en\">add accessibility information</a> for their business profiles to help users needing stair-free access find them on Google Maps and Search.</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>With this feature “rollout”, it’s easier to find and contribute wheelchair accessibility information to Google Maps. That benefits everyone, from those of us using wheelchairs and parents pushing strollers to older adults with tired legs and people hauling heavy items. And in this time of COVID-19, it’s especially important to know before you go so that you won’t be stranded outside that pharmacy, grocery or restaurant.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <figure class=\"article-image--full article-module \">\n  <img alt=\"How to contribute accessibility information to Google Maps\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Accessible_Places_Contribute_UI.gif\" />\n  <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption h-c-page\">\n   <div class=\"rich-text\">\n    <p>Anyone can contribute accessibility information to Google Maps</p>\n   </div>\n  </figcaption>\n </figure>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>To get wheelchair accessibility information more prominently displayed in Google Maps, update your app to the latest version, go to Settings, select “Accessibility,” and turn on “Accessible Places.” The feature is available on both Android and iOS.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>We’re also rolling out an update that allows people using iOS devices to more easily contribute accessibility information, joining the millions of Android users who have been sharing this type of information on Maps. <a href=\"https://www.localguidesconnect.com/t5/General-Discussion/How-to-answer-accessibility-questions-on-Google-Maps/td-p/26\">This guide</a>&nbsp;has tips for rating accessibility, in case you’re not sure what counts as being “accessible.” We invite everyone to switch on Accessible Places and contribute accessibility information to help people in your community.</p>\n  <p></p>\n  <h3>A Maps milestone, built on a movement</h3>\n  <p>This launch is a milestone in our journey to build a better, more helpful map for everyone, which includes recent efforts to help people find accessible <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/building-map-everyone/\">places</a>, <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/introducing-wheelchair-accessible-routes-transit-navigation/\">transit routes</a> and <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/better-maps-for-people-with-vision-impairments/\">walking directions</a>. Our work wouldn’t be possible without the decades of advocacy from those who have fought for equal access for people with disabilities. Were it not for them, there would be far fewer accessible places for Google Maps to show.</p>\n  <p>The Accessible Places feature is starting to rollout for Google Maps users in Australia, Japan, the United Kingdom and the United States, with support for additional countries on the way.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <figure class=\"article-image--full article-module \">\n  <img alt=\"How to turn on Accessible Places\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Accessible_Places_User_UI.gif\" />\n  <figcaption class=\"article-image__caption h-c-page\">\n   <div class=\"rich-text\">\n    <p>Use the Accessible Places feature to see accessibility information more prominently displayed in Google Maps</p>\n   </div>\n  </figcaption>\n </figure>\n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 21 May 2020 16:30:00 +0000","feedId":591,"bgimg":"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Accessible_Places_Contribute_UI.gif","linkMd5":"9019abdbed5efa8d9f9f177932b09f09","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Accessible_Places_Contribute_UI.gif":null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Accessible_Places_User_UI.gif":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/SbSV?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn10@2020_2/2020/08/16/12-12-00-698_4bbeb52263385580.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/SbSV?i=UBA4ofWZBsk:GJMamyfjaKk:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn45@2020_1/2020/08/16/12-12-02-809_2a737eb3f8e484c1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/blogspot/SbSV/~4/UBA4ofWZBsk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn5@2020_1/2020/08/16/12-11-59-567_8ed5fcf0e3247036.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:11:59","title":"No address? No problem. Share your location using Plus Codes","link":"https://blog.google/products/maps/an-address-for-everywhere-plus-codes/","description":"<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>For many of us, it’s easy to take addresses for granted. We order products online, and they show up at our doorstep. In an emergency, we give our address to an ambulance or fire truck, and they quickly get to us. But what happens when you don’t have an address and you need to direct someone to your current location?&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>More than 2 billion people on the planet—about 25 percent of us or more —either don’t have an address or have an address that isn’t easy to locate. To tackle this challenge, we launched <a href=\"https://plus.codes/\">Plus Codes</a> in 2015. Plus Codes are simple, easy to use digital addresses derived from latitude and longitude coordinates. They can be used to uniquely identify any location, from a rural home out on a prairie to a small shop stall on a nameless street.</p>\n  <p>Today we’ve made it easier for anyone with an Android device to share their location using Plus Codes in Google Maps. People who use Google Maps might be familiar with the blue dot that represents their current location. Simply tap the blue dot to get a Plus Code for your current location that can be shared with others as easily as giving them a phone number.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"Tap the blue dot to get a Plus Code\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Plus_Codes_blue_dot.gif\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <h3>Plus Codes: free, digital address for anywhere</h3>\n  <p>A Plus Code is a simple alphanumeric code which can be combined with a locality (for example: FWM8+V9, Ibadan, Nigeria). They look like a regular address, but with a short code where a street name or number would be. Beyond using the blue dot, you can also find the Plus Code for a location by tapping and holding the map to drop a pin at a location you want a Plus Code for.</p>\n  <p>Plus Codes are searchable on Google Maps and even Google Search, meaning everywhere on the planet can now be uniquely identified.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>These digital location identifiers are free to use, available offline and can be printed on paper, posters and signs. The technology to generate Plus Codes is also <a href=\"https://opensource.google/projects/open-location-code\">open source</a>, which means the technology is easy and free to use, so anyone can see how the technology works and develop their own applications for any use case.</p>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-image_full_width\">\n <div class=\"article-module h-c-page\">\n  <div class=\"h-c-grid\">\n   <figure class=\"article-image--large h-c-grid__col h-c-grid__col--6 h-c-grid__col--offset-3 \">\n    <img alt=\"About Plus Codes\" src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/About_Plus_Codes.gif\" />\n   </figure>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <h3>A helpful tool for emergency and crisis situations&nbsp;</h3>\n  <p>Plus Codes can be especially helpful for people and organizations in emergency and crisis response scenarios. If you’ve ever been in an emergency, you know that being able to share your location for help to easily find you is critical. Yet in many places in the world, organizations struggle with this challenge on a daily basis.&nbsp;</p>\n  <p>With Plus Codes, not only can people share their location quickly even without an address, but they can now do so by simply opening up Google Maps and tapping on the blue dot to view, copy and share their Plus Code location. A Plus Code can then be entered into Google Maps to help locate and navigate to that location.</p>\n  <p>Digital locations through Plus Codes means that everywhere now has an easily identifiable location, saving time and getting resources there when it really matters. Not having an address should no longer be a barrier to easily sharing your location with service providers, guiding them to you when you most need them.</p>\n  <p>Download the latest version of the Google Maps Android app over the coming weeks to try out the new update.</p>\n </div>\n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 28 May 2020 16:00:00 class=\"block-paragraph\">\n <div class=\"rich-text\">\n  <p>As a program manager for Street View, I’ve had the opportunity to work in more than 20 countries around the world, collecting <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/maps/google-maps-101-how-imagery-powers-our-map/\">imagery</a> that transports people to new places and powers Google Maps.&nbsp;</p>\n  <br />\n  <p>You can even find my blurred face from time to time in Street View. I’ve trekked a <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@22.9866607,53.7748954,2a,83.9y,153.29h,95.35t/data=!3m6!1e1!3m4!1sS48kHSyJQDcyOmoh21309A!2e0!7i13312!8i6656\">desert in Abu Dhabi</a> (with a camel no less) and walked around the <a href=\"https://www.google.com/maps/@29.9773355,31.1333187,2a,75y,276.44h,102.52t/data=!3m6!1e1!3m4!1sPZQhpxntkeOXyC8YMeCAvg!2e0!7i13312!8i6656\">Great Pyramids of Giza</a> (I’m the blurred face to the right).
